# C# and .NET Essential Training

> Microsoft .NET is a modern, cross-platform framework for developing applications for the web, desktop, and mobile devices. This course gives an introduction to some of the features of .NET that makes building applications easier, more performant, and more productive. Veteran technologist Joe Marini demonstrates how to use built-in capabilities of .NET such as string processing, data collection typ

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training) | 2h 22m | Intermediate | 45K learners

#### .NET: The everywhere framework
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-the-everywhere-framework?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-the-everywhere-framework?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Joe] The .NET platform has come a long way over the past 20 years since it was first introduced.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-the-everywhere-framework?u=76281980&t=5)** What started out as a runtime for desktop apps on Windows has become a cross-platform multiple form factor framework that gives developers the ability to create apps that run almost anywhere while sharing the same core sets of capabilities and features.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-the-everywhere-framework?u=76281980&t=20)** Hi, I'm Joe Marini, and I've been developing software for some of the biggest companies in Silicon Valley for more than 30 years.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-the-everywhere-framework?u=76281980&t=26)** In this course we'll learn about some of the features that .NET provides that can be used in any application that targets the platform.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-the-everywhere-framework?u=76281980&t=34)** We'll see how to work with strings, create, write and read information from files and directories, work with application data like numbers and dates, and even process information using regular expressions.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-the-everywhere-framework?u=76281980&t=47)** The .NET framework is everywhere today, which means that your apps can be everywhere, too.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-the-everywhere-framework?u=76281980&t=51)** Let's get started learning about the .NET framework using C#.

#### What you should know
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-you-should-know?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Before we begin the course, there are some concepts that you should already be familiar with.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=5)** In this course, I'm going to be introducing the .NET platform and some of the features it provides for building cross-platform applications, and I'll be using the C Sharp programming language along with the Visual Studio Code developer tool from Microsoft.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=19)** You can use regular Visual Studio as well if you're on Windows, but as of the recording of this course, Visual Studio 2022 on the Mac doesn't yet fully support .NET 6.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=30)** So to make things easy, I'll just use VS Code along with the command line for this course, so you could follow along easily whether you're on Mac, Windows, or Linux.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=39)** You don't need to have any prior experience with .NET, but this is not the place to start if you don't have any programming experience.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=46)** To take this course, you should at least have some knowledge of the basics of programming, such as what variables are, and how to use functions and so on.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=55)** If you need to brush up on your basic programming knowledge, then consider taking Programming Foundations: Fundamentals, or [[Programming Foundations- Object-Oriented Design]] first.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=66)** I'm also going to assume that you at least have some basic experience with C Sharp.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=71)** Even though this is an introductory course to .NET, again, this is not the place to start if you don't already know some C Sharp.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=78)** If you need to get up to speed with C Sharp, then consider taking the Learning C Sharp course.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=84)** And finally, since we're going to be using Visual Studio Code in this course, you might want to consider watching some of the great Visual Studio Code related courses, if you need to familiarize yourself with this tool such as Visual Studio Essential Training.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=97)** When you feel comfortable with each of these subjects, you're ready to proceed.

#### Installing .NET

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=0)** - If you're installing .NET on Windows or Mac then you have a couple of options open to you.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=6)** This page in the Microsoft documentation provides all the instructions needed to get .NET installed on your computer.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=13)** For Mac and Windows.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=15)** The easiest way is probably to just install Visual Studio which will take care of the process for you.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=21)** If you're using a different editor, such as VS Code then you might need to install .NET separately.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=27)** So let's begin by checking to see if your system already has .NET installed.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=31)** On your computer, whether it's Mac, Windows, or Linux, open a terminal window and then enter the command dotnet--version.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=41)** And you can see that when I run this command I have .NET six on my computer as the current version of .NET.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=48)** Now, if you didn't get a result that looks like this or if you got an error message then you'll need to install the .NET Framework.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=55)** If you already have .NET installed, then make sure the current version is six because the exercises in this course are built to work with version six of .NET.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=65)** Now different .NET versions can be installed side by side with each other, and you can check to see which SDKs you have by typing dotnet--list-sdks.

>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=86)** So if you want to install .NET manually then let's go back to that link.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=90)** So here on this page, right?
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/installing-dot-net?u=76281980&t=92)** You can click on the appropriate link for your machine.

#### Tour of CoderPad
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] This course includes automated code challenges that appear when you click on the challenge links in the course's table of contents.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=8)** Each challenge includes instructions and a couple of code editors you can use to create and test your own solution to the challenge.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=16)** These challenges are hosted by CoderPad and they appear in the same area of the course page where you watch the course's videos.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=23)** We recommend using a desktop browser for the best experience with code challenges, but you can use the LinkedIn Learning mobile app if you prefer.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=32)** The code challenge has four areas.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=35)** In the top left, you will find the instructions for completing the challenge, a code editor for you to create your answer in the top right, another code editor where you can see how your code is being used in the bottom right and a console for output in the bottom left.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=54)** You can use these drag handles to allocate screen space as you like, and you can see that I can resize each of these quadrants as I like.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=63)** And to get even more horizontal space for your code editors, you can collapse the course's table of contents on the left.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=71)** Each challenge has instructions that include a description of the challenge and the challenge's parameters and desired result.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=79)** Depending on the challenge, you will see some additional information in the instructions, such as an explanation of the parameters that your code will be given, along with some examples of what the expected output might look like, and you might even see a little hint down here in the lower left.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=98)** You will create your answer in the top right code editor.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=102)** There are comments in the starting code showing you where to put your solution, and then you will click on test my code, you'll see a message indicating whether your code returned a successful result.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=115)** So I'm going to go ahead and demo the existing state of this editor with the obvious wrong answer in there and when I click on test my code, you can see that it runs my code.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=125)** And over here in the console output, we can see that, oh, well that's not the expected result.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=130)** My code returned zero.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=133)** So obviously that's wrong.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=136)** The show expected result and show hints variables determine whether you see the expected result and any hints.

>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=149)** I'm going to change each of these to true, because I need some extra help.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=155)** Alright, so then I'll click on test my code again.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=159)** Alright, and now we can see that I got the error message, because again, my answer's wrong.
>

>

> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/tour-of-coderpad?u=76281980&t=236)** So I'll make the proper answer 25.

>

### 1. Overview of .NET

> [[#Table of Contents|↑ Back to Table of Contents]]

#### What is .NET?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-is-dot-net?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-is-dot-net?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] So what exactly is .NET?
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-is-dot-net?u=76281980&t=2)** .NET is a free, open source developer platform that runs on multiple different operating systems.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-is-dot-net?u=76281980&t=8)** It was first launched in 2001, and originally, it ran only on Windows, but has since been expanded to Mac, Linux, iOS, Android, gaming systems like Xbox, and even the cloud.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-is-dot-net?u=76281980&t=20)** The .NET platform can be programmed with a variety of languages, including C#, Visual Basic, F#, and of course the most popular open source ones, like Python, PHP, and C++.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-is-dot-net?u=76281980&t=32)** .NET presents a modern programming architecture that handles many of the more mundane programming tasks automatically for the developer, such as managing program memory.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-is-dot-net?u=76281980&t=43)** Conceptually, you can think of .NET as being a runtime layer between your apps and the operating systems and form factors that they run on.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-is-dot-net?u=76281980&t=52)** .NET provides a full set of services that apps need in order to complete their tasks and get their work done, as well as support for .NET enabled languages, like we saw previously, and the CLR, or the common language runtime, which enables the cross-platform abilities of the .NET platform.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-is-dot-net?u=76281980&t=71)** And as I mentioned, you can build many different kinds of apps with it, from desktop and mobile to web and cloud-based services.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-is-dot-net?u=76281980&t=79)** Now, obviously this is a lot more than can fit in just one course.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-is-dot-net?u=76281980&t=83)** For this course, we're going to be focusing on using C# and working with some of the common services provided by .NET.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/what-is-dot-net?u=76281980&t=90)** To keep things simple, we'll be building desktop console applications that run in the terminal, but you can of course, use all of the concepts presented in this course in other types of applications as well.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Env Vars:** net (9), php (1), clr (1)
> **CLI Commands:** python (1), php (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (2)
> **Code Keywords:** for . (1)
> **Code Identifiers:** ios (1)
> **Tools:** terminal (1)
> **Analogies:** such as (1)
> **Speakers:** - [instructor] (1)

#### Basic .NET data types
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Before we start working with the .NET SDK, it's important to understand the basic data types that are supported by the platform and the difference between value types and reference types.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=12)** .NET supports several built-in types.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=15)** The integral numeric types include bytes, integers and long integers.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=21)** Next are the floating point number types, such as float, double and decimal.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=27)** The character type consists of a single text character.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=31)** Boolean can be either true or false.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=34)** And there are some built-in reference types as well, such as the string, which is a sequence of characters, and the object type, which represents a complex object in memory.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=44)** Now, this is not an exhaustive list of all the detailed data types in .NET, but it represents most of the types that you will usually work with.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=52)** And as I mentioned, there are both value types and reference types.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=56)** Value types directly contain the value that they represent.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=61)** And examples of value types include the built-in number types, and booleans and characters, and so on, and even some complex types like enumerations and structs.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=72)** When a value type is used as a function argument, a copy of the value is passed to the function.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=79)** And we'll see why this is important.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=81)** Reference types are a little bit different.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=83)** They contain a reference to the value they represent.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=86)** And what this means is that two different variables can refer to the same value in memory.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=93)** And some examples of these types are strings, objects and records.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=98)** So let's open our exercise code and take a look at some example.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=104)** So here in VS Code, in the Start folder, we'll go to Overview and DataTypes.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=111)** And let's open the program file. Right.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=115)** So here I have some code that declares a variety of variable types, right?
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=119)** This integers, characters, floats, decimal, and so on.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=124)** And notice that I use the characters f and m for the literal float and decimal values.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=131)** You can also use the default keyword to assign whatever the default value is for that particular data type.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/basic-dot-net-data-types?u=76281980&t=139)** So for example, the default value for an integer is zero.
>

#### .NET garbage collection
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The .NET platform uses what's called a Managed Memory Model similar to other platforms like Java.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=7)** In other words, the platform takes care of managing the blocks of memory that your program creates and reclaiming them when they are no longer in use.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=17)** The garbage collection also works to make sure that when your program allocates memory for use that memory is created efficiently within the managed heap for your program.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=27)** The heap is an area of system memory reserved for your program where your program's objects are kept safe from other programs and processes.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=35)** So all of this happens automatically.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=37)** This frees the developer from having to manually keep track of allocations and then remembering to dispose of each one.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=45)** So, there are a few exceptions to this process and usually these are associated with operating system resources, like files and network connections that your program needs to explicitly clean up on its own.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=57)** So, the garbage collector knows how to dispose of the managed object that refers to one of these resources but it doesn't have enough information to manage the resource itself.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=67)** But for the most part, your program can rely on the garbage collector to efficiently manage memory for your app.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=73)** So, let's take a look at how this works conceptually.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=76)** So let's imagine that this box represents your program's memory and as your program executes, it's going to create objects in memory, right represented by these boxes.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=85)** Now, over time, some of these objects will no longer be needed, at which point the garbage collector marks them as being ready for collection.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=93)** Then the collector will reclaim these objects and make the memory available for use by other parts of your program.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=100)** So let's see this in action in a real program.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=104)** So, here in Visual Studio Code I've got my sample program open and I have a local function called do big operation or it's called, here it is, it's do some big operation and it allocates a one megabyte array of bites.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=121)** And I'm going to use the garbage collector's get total memory function which is this function right here, let me collapse that down so we can see more, so this get total memory function right here shows me how much memory my app is using.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=136)** So the GC object right here is part of the system namespace, and since this is .NET 6, I don't need to explicitly include that name space in order to use it.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=148)** The rest of my code is going to write out the amount of memory being used when it starts, and then I'm going to call this function, right, called do some big operation and we'll see how much memory gets used up and then after that function completes, I'm going to explicitly call the garbage collector to force a garbage collection, so I'm going to write GC.collect.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=171)** Now, to be perfectly clear, your application will probably never need to do this.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=176)** This function is provided mainly for testing purposes, all right, the garbage collector collects memory whenever it needs to, so you'll never have to actually call this function, this is only for demonstration purposes.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=189)** So, let's go ahead and run the program, going to open up my terminal and I'm going to write dotnet run.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=200)** Okay, so you can see that when the program starts, it says that the allocated memory is 67,552 bytes, all right, so I'll hit the return key and then after I do that giant allocation, which is right here, this megabyte, you can see that now the allocated memory is, what is that?
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=218)** That's 1.1 megabytes it looks like, so, that memory usage jumps because of the big allocation and when the function completes, this local variable right here called myArray goes out of scope and it's no longer used by the program.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=234)** So, the garbage collector notices this and so when I hit return again, you can see that after the GC.collect function gets called, the garbage collector reclaims all that memory.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=245)** And you can see that the memory usage drops back down again.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=248)** Now it doesn't go back all the way to the original value because other parts of the .NET framework have been invoked and are now in use, but it's by a significant amount.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=258)** So, here's where it started, here's that big allocation, and then after I call collect, we go back down to 100K.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/dot-net-garbage-collection?u=76281980&t=265)** So, again, I want to just point out, your program will never need to manually collect the memory using the garbage collector command, this all happens automatically, this is just a demonstration, but this illustrates how the memory is automatically managed for your app.

> **[6:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/parsing-numbers?u=76281980&t=408)** So let's try to parse the 1.45 number as an int.
>
> **[6:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/parsing-numbers?u=76281980&t=419)** All right, now, we know that's going to fail.
>
> **[7:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/parsing-numbers?u=76281980&t=422)** So let's go ahead and run this again and sure enough, you can see that now the result is false for a tri-parse when we try to parse this floating point number as an integer.
>
> **[7:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/parsing-numbers?u=76281980&t=433)** So by using the parse and tri-parse methods, you can easily convert string data into basic built-in data types.

#### Solution: Files and directories
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Okay, let's review my solution to this challenge and you can compare it to yours along the way.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=11)** So in my code, I start with a couple of string contents that contain the name of the folder that's going to be scanned along with name of the results file that's going to be created.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=23)** These are followed by the variables I'm going to use to build the information that we need to summarize things like the number of each file type, the total file count, total number of bytes, and so on.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=37)** This function is office file, determines if a given name is an office file.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=45)** Now it's a very simplistic test that just looks at the suffix of the file name to see if it ends in a known file extension for office files.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=52)** Next, we get into the main algorithm for the program.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=55)** So I create a DirectoryInfo object for the folder that we're going to scan.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=61)** Then, the code uses the enumerate files function to iterate over each file in the directory.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=69)** And each time the function will return a FileInfo object that contains information about that particular file.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=77)** The program passes that file name to the IsOfficeFile function.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=81)** And if it returns true, then we increase the total file count along with the total file size, using the length property of the file info to get the number of bytes for that file.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=93)** The process is then repeated based on what type of office file this is.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=99)** And in each case the code counts that particular type and size.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=104)** So when the loop completes the code calls the CreateText function to create the results file and then each piece of data is written out.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=115)** And for the numbers, notice that I'm using the string formatting syntax that we learned about earlier in the course to format each these numbers as a regular number with zero precision which will give me the commas for the thousand separators.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=130)** And yeah, that's pretty much it.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=132)** So take a few moments here to compare your code with mine and think about ways you might extend it.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/solution-files-and-directories?u=76281980&t=138)** So, for example, how would you change the code to count the total number of both office and non-office files and add the total bytes of all the files to the results but keeping just the office file count the same.

#### Using RegEx timeouts
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/using-regex-timeouts?u=76281980)

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/using-regex-timeouts?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] One of the things you need to be really careful about when working with regular expressions is that they can be an unexpected source of potential security issues or other program problems.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/using-regex-timeouts?u=76281980&t=10)** So for example, if your program works with text that comes from outside your app or outside your organization, then it's not that hard to create a text string that can hang your program resulting in a type of denial of service attack.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-and-dot-net-essential-training/using-regex-timeouts?u=76281980&t=24)** So one way to help guard against this is by using timeouts to make sure that your Regexes don't hang the program.
